Parsing [sent. 1132 len. 61]: During the time that Belgium was attached to the Netherlands , the king , with the prince and princess of Orange , came here almost every year , bringing with them , of course , a great number of the nobility ; but now the nobility have deserted the court ; and when Leopold came here , no one followed .
Parsing [sent. 1133 len. 11]: He was disgusted , and remained but a few days .
Parsing [sent. 1134 len. 63]: The Prussians used also to resort very much to Spa ; but the king of Prussia finding that so many young men were ruined at the gaming-tables , and so much distress occasioned by it , with a most fatherly despotism , has refused all the officers permission to visit Spa , and has forbidden the medical men to recommend the waters .
Parsing [sent. 1135 len. 105]: The Russians also flocked in great numbers to Spa ; but the emperor , although very indifferent about their losing their money , is very particular about his subjects gaining revolutionary opinions ; and Spa being in a revolutionary country , has been condemned : they may just as well ask to go to Siberia , for that would probably be their route ; and lastly , there is one more cause which , these two last seasons , has had a powerful effect , neither more nor less than a certain book , called the '' _ Bubbles of the Brunnen _ . ''
Parsing [sent. 1136 len. 42]: I say for the last two seasons , for its influence will not extend to a third , as hundreds and hundreds who have gone to the Baths with the intention of passing this season , have already returned in disgust .
Parsing [sent. 1137 len. 5]: A word upon this .
Parsing [sent. 1138 len. 44]: When Sir George Head published his `` Bubbles , '' he set people almost as mad as they were during the great `` Bubble Mania ; '' and like all the mining and other associations , they have proved but bubbles at last .
Parsing [sent. 1139 len. 59]: It is said that one hundred and thirty-five thousand passports were taken out last year to go up the Rhine , by people who wished to see the pigs go through their daily manoeuvres , to an unearthly solo on the horn , and to witness the decapitation of the Seltzer-water bottles , which were condemned as traitors .
Parsing [sent. 1140 len. 35]: Now , so large an influx of people to these German watering-places could have but one effect ; that of a glorious harvest to the innkeepers , and those who had lodgings to let .
Parsing [sent. 1141 len. 34]: The prices , at these places , have now become so enormous , that three florins have been asked for a single bed , and everything else has risen in the same proportion .
Parsing [sent. 1142 len. 54]: The reaction has now begun to take place , and every day and every hour we have carriages returning through Liege , and other towns , from these watering-places , the occupants holding up their hands , quite forgetting the pigs and bottles , and only exclaiming against extortion , and everything German .
Parsing [sent. 1143 len. 30]: They have paid too dear for their whistle , as Franklin used to say ; the bubble has burst , and they look with regret at their empty purses .
Parsing [sent. 1144 len. 14]: And yet , all that Head said in his amusing book was true .
Parsing [sent. 1145 len. 21]: He rambled through a verdant and unfrequented lane , and described what he felt as he stopped to pick blackberries .
Parsing [sent. 1146 len. 39]: An immense multitude have followed him , the green lane has been beaten down into a high road , and , as for blackberries , they are only to be procured at the price of peaches in May .
Parsing [sent. 1147 len. 16]: And now let us reflect whether the bubble will not also burst with the Germans .
Parsing [sent. 1148 len. 17]: Formerly they were contented with moderate profits , and received their visitors with humility and thankfulness .
Parsing [sent. 1149 len. 41]: Now , that they have suddenly made large profits , they have become independent and unceremonious ; and , like most people , because they have reaped a golden harvest for two years , they anticipate that it will continue .
Parsing [sent. 1150 len. 53]: The value of property at these places has risen , speculations have been entered into on a large scale , provisions and the necessaries of life have become dear ; new houses are building against time , and the proprietors smoke their pipes with becoming gravity , calculating upon their future gains .
Parsing [sent. 1151 len. 39]: But the company will fall off more and more each succeeding year , although the speculations will continue ; for people always find a good reason for a bad season , and anticipate a better one the next .
Parsing [sent. 1152 len. 58]: At last , they will find that they are again deserted , and property will sink in value to nothing ; the reaction will have fully taken place , prices will fall even lower than they were at first ; honesty and civility will be reassumed , although , probably , the principal will have been lost .
Parsing [sent. 1153 len. 16]: Thus will the bubble burst with them , as it has already with deserted Spa .
Parsing [sent. 1154 len. 22]: But when all idle people shall have visited all the bubbling fountains of Germany , where are they to go next ?
Parsing [sent. 1155 len. 29]: There are some very nice springs in Iceland not yet patronised ; but although the springs there are hot , the Springs , vernally speaking , are cold .
Parsing [sent. 1156 len. 48]: I can inform travellers where they will find out something new , and I advise them to proceed to the boiling springs at Saint Michael 's , one of the Western isles , and which are better worth seeing than all the springs that Germany can produce .
Parsing [sent. 1157 len. 10]: I will act as _ guide de voyage _ .
Parsing [sent. 1158 len. 60]: When you land at Saint Michael 's , you will find yourself in one of the dirtiest towns in the world , and will put up at one of the worst hotels ; however , you will have to pay just as dear as if lodged at the Clarendon , and fed at the _ Rocher de Cancale _ .
Parsing [sent. 1159 len. 10]: The town contains many inhabitants , but more pigs .
Parsing [sent. 1160 len. 10]: German pigs are not to be compared to them .
Parsing [sent. 1161 len. 65]: You must then hire donkeys and ascend to the mountains , and after a hot ride , you will arrive at a small valley in the centre of the mountains , which was once the crater of a volcano , but is now used by nature as a kettle , in which she keeps hot water perpetually boiling for those who may require it .
Parsing [sent. 1162 len. 40]: There you will behold the waters bubbling and boiling in all directions , throwing up huge white columns of smoke , brought out in strong relief by the darker sides of the mountains which rear their heads around you .
Parsing [sent. 1163 len. 44]: The ground you tread upon trembles as you walk ; you feel that it is only a thin crust , and that in a moment you may sink into the vast cauldron below , and have a hot bath without paying for it .
Parsing [sent. 1164 len. 56]: Continue along the valley , and you will find lakes of still , deadly-cold water , with hot springs at their verge , throwing the smoke over their surface , while they pour in their boiling water as if they would fain raise the temperature ; depositing sulphur in cakes and crystals in their course .
Parsing [sent. 1165 len. 68]: And in another spot there is a dark , unfathomable hole , called the Devil 's Mouth : you approach it , and you hear low moanings and rumblings , as if nature had the stomach-ache ; and then you will have a sudden explosion , and a noise like thunder , and a shower of mud will be thrown out to a distance of several yards .
Parsing [sent. 1166 len. 43]: Wait again ; you will again hear the moans and rumblings , and in about three minutes the explosion and the discharge will again take place ; and thus has this eternal diarrhoea continued ever since the memory or tradition of man .
Parsing [sent. 1167 len. 61]: Yet , upon this apparently insecure and dangerous spot have been erected houses and baths , and it is resorted to by the fashionables of Saint Michael 's , who wish , by its properties , to get rid of certain cutaneous disorders : for the whole air is loaded with sulphurous vapour , as the eternal pot keeps boiling .
Parsing [sent. 1168 len. 111]: Observe the advantages of this place : -- you may have a bath as hot as you please , as cold as you please , or you may have a mud _ douche _ , if you have that buffalo propensity ; and then you will have to rough it , which is so delightful ; you will find little or nothing to eat , and plenty of bedfellows in all their varieties , a burning sun , and a dense atmosphere , and you will be very delighted to get back again , which , after all , is the _ summum bonum _ to be obtained by travel .
Parsing [sent. 1169 len. 39]: Not very far from this valley of hot water there is another valley , containing four small lakes , and in those lakes are found the most beautiful gold and silver fish , perhaps , in the world .
Parsing [sent. 1170 len. 20]: How they came there , Heaven only knows ; but I mention this because there is a curious coincidence .
Parsing [sent. 1171 len. 16]: These lakes are known by the name of the Quadre Cidade , or four cities .
Parsing [sent. 1172 len. 50]: Now , if my readers will recollect , in the `` Arabian Nights , '' there is a story of a valley with four lakes , which were once four cities , and that in these lakes were fish of various beautiful colours , who were once the inhabitants .
Parsing [sent. 1173 len. 76]: If I recollect right , when the fish were caught and put into the frying-pan , they jumped up and made a speech ; -LRB- so would fish now-a-days , if they were not mute ;-RRB- and the story is told by a prince , whose lower extremities are turned into black marble , very convenient , certainly , if he dined out every day , as he had only his upper toilet to complete .
Parsing [sent. 1174 len. 60]: This coincidence appeared to me to be very curious , and had I had time and opportunity I certainly should have fried four of these unfortunate fish , to ascertain whether they were of the real breed spoken of in the Arabian Tales , of the authenticity of which no one , I presume , will venture to doubt .
Parsing [sent. 1175 len. 3]: CHAPTER NINETEEN .
Parsing [sent. 1176 len. 5]: Spa , July 15 .
Parsing [sent. 1177 len. 14]: What a curious history might be afforded by Spa and its gaming tables !
Parsing [sent. 1178 len. 74]: When Spa was in its glory , when crowned heads met and dukes were forced to remain in their carriages for want of accommodation , when it was the focus of all that was _ recherche _ and brilliant , for Spa was so before the French revolution , the gaming tables were a source of immense profit ; and to whom do you imagine that a great portion of the profits belonged ?
Parsing [sent. 1179 len. 27]: -- to no less a person than the most sacred and puissant prince , the Bishop of Liege , who derived a great revenue from them .
Parsing [sent. 1180 len. 37]: But it would appear as if there was a judgment upon this anomalous secular property , for these gaming-tables were the cause of the Prince Bishop losing all , and being driven out of his territories .
Parsing [sent. 1181 len. 27]: There were two gaming establishments at Spa , the Redoubt in the town , and the Vauxhall about a quarter of a mile outside of it .
Parsing [sent. 1182 len. 32]: The Redoubt is a fine building , with splendid ball-rooms and a theatre , but you must go _ through the gaming-rooms _ to enter either the ball-room or the theatre .
Parsing [sent. 1183 len. 34]: The Vauxhall has no theatre , but the rooms are even more spacious ; but when Spa was at its zenith , even these two immense edifices were barely sufficient for the company .
Parsing [sent. 1184 len. 48]: Both these establishments were under the same proprietors , and it so happened that the English nobility , who were always a very strong party here , were displeased with the conduct of the lessees , and immediately raised funds for the building of a second Vauxhall .
Parsing [sent. 1185 len. 53]: The bishop ordered the building to be discontinued , but , as by the privileges granted by former bishops , this was a violation of the rights of the Liegeois , his order was disregarded , and the Vauxhall now known by the name of _ the Vauxhall _ , was finished .
Parsing [sent. 1186 len. 35]: When finished , the bishop would not permit it to be opened , but his commands being disregarded , he came down with two hundred soldiers and two pieces of cannon and took possession .
Parsing [sent. 1187 len. 19]: This created a revolution , and the bishop was ultimately obliged to fly his territory and seek assistance .
Parsing [sent. 1188 len. 48]: The Prussians marched an army into the city , and there was apparent submission , but as soon as they quitted , the insurrection again took place , and the bishop was forced again to solicit aid from the Austrians , for Prussia would no longer interfere .
Parsing [sent. 1189 len. 40]: Metternich , who was so fond of legitimacy that he considered the gaming-tables a legitimate source of revenue to the apostle , marched in an Austrian army , and hundreds were slaughtered that the bishop might obtain his rights .
Parsing [sent. 1190 len. 55]: Such was the state of affairs when the French revolution broke out and convulsed Europe , and the province of Liege was among the very first to receive with open arms the _ bonnet rouge _ and to join themselves with France , and thus did the bishop lose his beautiful province for ever .
Parsing [sent. 1191 len. 14]: As far as Liege was concerned , the French revolution proved a blessing .
Parsing [sent. 1192 len. 32]: It certainly was a disgraceful finale to an ecclesiastical power , which , as I have before mentioned , had formerly led the van in the march of Christianity and liberty .
Parsing [sent. 1193 len. 89]: But it appears that the clergy are fated to have an interest in these gaming-tables , the stipend of the English resident clergyman being , even now , paid out of their profits ; for when Belgium was made over to the Netherlands , King William assumed his right to the bishop 's former share of the profits of the tables , and of course brought as many people down here as he could to _ lose their money _ , as he pocketed his _ thirds _ .
Parsing [sent. 1194 len. 33]: Since the revolution , Leopold is in King William 's shoes , but there are little or no profits , as Spa is deserted and the expenses of the establishments are great .
Parsing [sent. 1195 len. 29]: Perhaps there is no spot of ground in Europe -- I will not except Paris -- where so much money has been lost by gaming as at Spa .
Parsing [sent. 1196 len. 18]: I was walking with a friend who pointed out to me a small pavilion in a garden .
Parsing [sent. 1197 len. 33]: `` There , '' says he , `` the Prince of Orange , who played very deeply , lost to a Spanish gentleman those very jewels that were pretended to be stolen .
Parsing [sent. 1198 len. 17]: It was well got up in the papers , but that is the real truth . ''
Parsing [sent. 1199 len. 77]: How far it may be the truth or not , I can not pretend to say , and only know that in Spa you can not pick your teeth without all the world knowing it , and that this is fully believed at Spa to be the real truth of the disappearance of the splendid jewels of the princess , which have since been redeemed from the Spanish gentleman , who now resides at the Hague .
Parsing [sent. 1200 len. 43]: Gaming has always been held up in abhorrence as a vice ; but it is rather a passion strongly implanted by nature , and abhorrent from the dreadful effects produced by its overpowering influence , than a vice _ per se _ .
Parsing [sent. 1201 len. 18]: Life itself is a lottery , and the best part of our life is passed in gambling .
Parsing [sent. 1202 len. 20]: It is difficult to draw the line between gambling and speculation , for every speculation is a gambling transaction .
Parsing [sent. 1203 len. 7]: Is not the merchant a gambler ?
Parsing [sent. 1204 len. 12]: in fact , is not every venture an act of gambling ?
Parsing [sent. 1205 len. 15]: As for the Stock Exchange , it is the very worst species of gambling .
Parsing [sent. 1206 len. 52]: All we can say is , that gambling may be legitimate or otherwise ; that is , there are species of gambling which may enrich the individual if he is fortunate , but whether it enriches him or not , at all events it is beneficial to the community at large .
Parsing [sent. 1207 len. 43]: A merchant speculates -- he sends out manufactures of every description : he fails , and is ruined : but the artisans have procured employment for their industry , and , although the merchant fails , the community at large has benefited .
Parsing [sent. 1208 len. 13]: This is legitimate gambling ; but do people in business stop there ?
Parsing [sent. 1209 len. 37]: No : they will agree to deliver so many thousands of casks of tallow or tons of hemp at such and such a time and at a certain price , whatever the price may then be .
Parsing [sent. 1210 len. 55]: They can not complete their engagement , and they are ruined ; but in this instance , which is simply termed speculation , we have quite as much gambling as if the money were at once laid down on the table , and the chances decided in an hour instead of so many months .
Parsing [sent. 1211 len. 32]: But there is this difference , that this party does not injure his character by such a transaction , whereas , if he lost his money at the gaming-table he would .
Parsing [sent. 1212 len. 29]: The English are , with the exception of the Americans , the most gambling nation under heaven ; naturally so , because they are the greatest mercantile nation .
Parsing [sent. 1213 len. 18]: The spirit of gambling is innate , and when directed into the proper channel it becomes enterprise .
Parsing [sent. 1214 len. 47]: It is doubtless a great moral error on the part of a government to encourage vice with the view of increasing the revenue , but , at the same time , there is no tax so well laid on as that which is imposed on vice .
Parsing [sent. 1215 len. 33]: Again , there are certain propensities in man which can not be overcome , and which , if attempted to be wholly eradicated by legal enactments , would occasion more evil still .
Parsing [sent. 1216 len. 43]: All that a judicious government can or should attempt to effect is , to restrain them within proper bounds , to regulate them , and as much as possible to keep them out of sight , that the virus may not extend .
Parsing [sent. 1217 len. 48]: It is well known , that certain houses are licensed by the magistrates , because , it being impossible to eradicate the vice , they can do no more than to separate it , that it may not be communicated to the healthier part of the community .
Parsing [sent. 1218 len. 39]: Now upon this principle , which is the true principle of sound legislation , I have often thought that it was a great error in our legislature when they consented to put down the public lotteries in England .
Parsing [sent. 1219 len. 32]: I am convinced that they were beneficial , acting as safety-valves to the gambling spirit of the nation , and that their prohibition has been productive of much crime and misery .
Parsing [sent. 1220 len. 21]: The spirit of gambling can not be eradicated ; it ought , therefore , to be kept within due bounds .
Parsing [sent. 1221 len. 36]: There was one great advantage in the English lottery ; it was drawn but once a year , and those who purchased the tickets were content to remain quiet until their success was made known .
Parsing [sent. 1222 len. 40]: The chances , although very distant , of so high a prize , satisfied the spirit of gambling ; if they lost , they purchased again , and waited patiently for another year , trusting to be more fortunate .
Parsing [sent. 1223 len. 17]: Now , although they gambled , they did not acquire the _ habit _ of gaming .
Parsing [sent. 1224 len. 12]: What has been the consequence since the lotteries have been abolished ?
Parsing [sent. 1225 len. 57]: that there are hells of every description established throughout the metropolis , from those which admit the stake of a shilling , to Crockford 's splendid Pandemonium ; and those who were formerly content with a lottery ticket , now pass their evenings away from their families , and ruin themselves in a very short time .
Parsing [sent. 1226 len. 7]: The lottery never ruined any one .
Parsing [sent. 1227 len. 39]: The sum staked might be large for the circumstances of the parties , but it was a yearly stake , and did not interfere with the industry , the profits , or the domestic happiness of the year .
Parsing [sent. 1228 len. 27]: One half the tradesmen who now appear in the `` Gazette , '' have been ruined by frequenting the low hells with which the metropolis abounds .
Parsing [sent. 1229 len. 17]: From the above considerations , I do not think it was advisable to abolish the lotteries .
Parsing [sent. 1230 len. 32]: The next question is one upon which I hesitate to offer an opinion ; but it is worthy of consideration how far it may be advisable to license and tax gaming-houses .
Parsing [sent. 1231 len. 21]: Were it possible to put them down altogether , the question need not be discussed ; but it is impossible .
Parsing [sent. 1232 len. 25]: Has any magistrate ventured to interfere with Crockford 's , where it is well known that the highest gaming is carried on every night ?
Parsing [sent. 1233 len. 16]: Are you not permitted to walk through the club at any hour of the day ?
Parsing [sent. 1234 len. 14]: Do they not have the tables exposed to the view of every one ?
Parsing [sent. 1235 len. 27]: Yet who has interfered , although you find that the smaller hells are constantly broken in upon , and the parties had up to the police-office ?
Parsing [sent. 1236 len. 8]: Are not the laws made for all ?
Parsing [sent. 1237 len. 21]: Is that an offence in the eyes of government in a poor man which is not one in the rich ?
Parsing [sent. 1238 len. 10]: Yet this is the case : and why so ?
Parsing [sent. 1239 len. 14]: Because the rich will game , and the government can not prevent them .
Parsing [sent. 1240 len. 16]: Has not a man a right to do as he pleases with his own money ?
Parsing [sent. 1241 len. 47]: You legalise the worst of gambling on the Stock Exchange , for a man can there risk what he can not pay : you can not control the gaming of the race-course , and yet you would prevent a man from gambling after his own fashion .
Parsing [sent. 1242 len. 18]: You wink at the higher classes ruining themselves , and you will not permit the middle classes .
Parsing [sent. 1243 len. 76]: Now the consequence of not having licensed tables is , that you have no control over them , and the public , who will play , are the dupes of rascals who cheat in every way : whereas , if a certain number were licensed and controlled , those who play would have a better chance , and the licensed tables taxed by government would take care to put down all others who were not .
Parsing [sent. 1244 len. 64]: We must legislate for society as it is , not as it ought to be ; and , as on other points , we have found it necessary to submit to the lesser evil of the two , it is a question whether in this also we might not do better by keeping within due bounds that which it is impossible to prevent .
Parsing [sent. 1245 len. 10]: I was amused with an anecdote told me to-day .
Parsing [sent. 1246 len. 13]: An Englishman and a Frenchman arrived at Spa in the same diligence .
Parsing [sent. 1247 len. 22]: They both took up their quarters at the same hotel , but from that moment appeared to have no further intimacy .
Parsing [sent. 1248 len. 8]: `` Do you see that fellow ? ''
Parsing [sent. 1249 len. 22]: would the Englishman say , pointing at the Frenchman , `` I know him , and he 's a confounded rogue .
Parsing [sent. 1250 len. 10]: I recommend you to be shy of him . ''
Parsing [sent. 1251 len. 6]: `` Voyez-vous cet Anglais ? ''
Parsing [sent. 1252 len. 9]: said the Frenchman as the Englishman passed by .
Parsing [sent. 1253 len. 11]: `` Gardez-vous en bien ; c'est un coquin superieur . ''
Parsing [sent. 1254 len. 69]: Thus did they continue to warn the company of each other , until the close of the season , when one fine day they both went off together in the diligence , leaving all their debts unpaid , and their trunks and portmanteaus for the benefit of the landlord of the hotel , who , on opening them , found them to contain nothing but stones and rubbish .
Parsing [sent. 1255 len. 21]: This was a new species of holy alliance , but the _ ruse _ was by no means ill advised .
Parsing [sent. 1256 len. 27]: When you hear a man constantly proclaiming the roguery of another , you are too apt to give him credit for honesty in his own person .
Parsing [sent. 1257 len. 29]: Thus , with those whom each party associated and dealt with , they obtained a credit for honesty , which enabled them to succeed in their roguish endeavours .
Parsing [sent. 1258 len. 3]: CHAPTER TWENTY .
Parsing [sent. 1259 len. 2]: Ostend .
Parsing [sent. 1260 len. 29]: From Spa to Liege , from Liege to Brussels , from Brussels to Ostend , how detestable it is to go over the same ground again and again !
Parsing [sent. 1261 len. 11]: only to be imposed upon and cheated again and again .
Parsing [sent. 1262 len. 13]: What a weary world this is , and what a rascally one !
Parsing [sent. 1263 len. 14]: How delightful a little honesty would be , by way of a change !
Parsing [sent. 1264 len. 28]: Of all the rascality spread like butter on bread over the surface of the globe , certainly the butter lies thicker on the confines of each territory .
Parsing [sent. 1265 len. 14]: There is a concentration of dishonesty at the ports of embarkation and debarkation .
Parsing [sent. 1266 len. 18]: Take London when you land from a steam-boat , or Dover , or Calais , or Ostend .
Parsing [sent. 1267 len. 11]: It is nothing but a system of extortion or over-reaching .
Parsing [sent. 1268 len. 4]: And why so ?
Parsing [sent. 1269 len. 29]: because in the hurry , the confusion , the sickness , and the ignorance of what is right , everything that is wrong can be practised with impunity .
Parsing [sent. 1270 len. 41]: These preyers upon mankind at the confines , remind you of the sharks in India , who always ply _ in the surf _ , where their motions can not be seen , and the unwary are invariably their prey .
Parsing [sent. 1271 len. 64]: I have knocked three down already , and one would imagine they would hasten for redress ; but they will not , for that would take hours , and during these hours they will lose the opportunity of making their harvest , so they get up again , and pocket the affront , that they may not lose time in filling their pockets .
Parsing [sent. 1272 len. 22]: Talking about roguery , there was a curious incident occurred some time back , in which a rascal was completely outwitted .
Parsing [sent. 1273 len. 26]: A bachelor gentleman , who was a very superior draftsman and caricaturist , was laid up in his apartments with the gout in both feet .
Parsing [sent. 1274 len. 28]: He could not move , but sat in an easy chair , and was wheeled by his servant in and out of his chamber to his sitting-room .
Parsing [sent. 1275 len. 20]: Now a certain well-known vagabond ascertained the fact , and watched until the servant was sent upon a message .
Parsing [sent. 1276 len. 21]: The servant came out of the front door , but left the area door open , communicating with the kitchen .
Parsing [sent. 1277 len. 29]: Down went the vagabond , entered the kitchen , and walked up stairs , where , as he anticipated , he found the gentleman quite alone and helpless .
Parsing [sent. 1278 len. 32]: `` I am sorry , sir , to see you in this situation , '' said the rogue ; `` you can not move , and your servant is out . ''
Parsing [sent. 1279 len. 4]: The gentleman stared .
Parsing [sent. 1280 len. 18]: `` It is excessively careless of you to leave yourself so exposed , for behold the consequences .
Parsing [sent. 1281 len. 48]: I take the liberty of removing this watch and these seals off the table , and putting them into my own pocket ; and , as I perceive your keys are here , I shall now open these drawers , and see what suits my purpose . ''
Parsing [sent. 1282 len. 3]: `` Oh !
Parsing [sent. 1283 len. 24]: pray help yourself , I beg , '' replied the gentleman , who was aware that he could do nothing to prevent him .
Parsing [sent. 1284 len. 47]: The rogue did so accordingly ; he found the plate in the sideboard drawer , and many other articles which suited him , and in about ten minutes , having made up his bundle , he made the gentleman a very low bow , and decamped .
Parsing [sent. 1285 len. 56]: But the gentleman had the use of his hands , and had not been idle ; he had taken an exact likeness of the thief with his pencil , and on his servant returning soon after , he despatched him immediately to Bow Street with the drawing , and an account of what had happened .
Parsing [sent. 1286 len. 31]: The likeness was so good , that the man was immediately identified by the runners , and was captured before he had time to dispose of a single article purloined .
Parsing [sent. 1287 len. 36]: He was brought to the gentleman in two hours afterwards , identified , the property found on him sworn to , and , in six weeks , he was on his passage to Botany Bay .
Parsing [sent. 1288 len. 4]: CHAPTER TWENTY ONE .
Parsing [sent. 1289 len. 4]: London , November .
Parsing [sent. 1290 len. 9]: We have the signs of the times here .
Parsing [sent. 1291 len. 19]: I peep through the fog and see quite enough to satisfy me that the prosperity is but partial .
Parsing [sent. 1292 len. 12]: Money in plenty , but lying in heaps -- not circulated .
Parsing [sent. 1293 len. 17]: Every one hugs his bag , and is waiting to see what the event may be .
Parsing [sent. 1294 len. 31]: Retrenchment is written up as evident as the prophetic words of fire upon the walls of Belshazzar 's palace -- _ To let -- to let -- to let _ .
Parsing [sent. 1295 len. 21]: Leave London in any direction , and you find the same mystical characters every one hundred yards of the road .
Parsing [sent. 1296 len. 25]: This beautiful villa , this cottage ornee , this capital house with pleasure-grounds , this mansion and park -- all -- all to let .
Parsing [sent. 1297 len. 23]: It is said that there are upwards of seven thousand of these country seats to let within twelve miles of the metropolis .
Parsing [sent. 1298 len. 41]: Again , look at the arms of the carriages which still roll through the streets , and you will perceive that if not with a coronet or supporters , nine out of ten have the widow 's _ lozenge _ .
Parsing [sent. 1299 len. 4]: And why so ?
Parsing [sent. 1300 len. 26]: because they belong to the widows of those who died in the times of plenty , and who left them large jointures upon their estates .
Parsing [sent. 1301 len. 36]: They , of course , can still support and even better support , the expense ; but the estates now yield but sufficient to pay the jointure , and the incumbent swallows up the whole .
Parsing [sent. 1302 len. 10]: And where are the real owners of the properties ?
Parsing [sent. 1303 len. 44]: At Paris , at Naples , at Brussels , if they can afford to be in a Capital -- if not , dispersed over Belgium , Switzerland , and Italy -- retrenching in other countries , or living more comfortably upon their incomes .
Parsing [sent. 1304 len. 45]: How many millions , for it does amount to millions , are now spent on the continent , enriching the people of other countries , and in all probability laying up for those countries the sinews for another war to be directed against England !
Parsing [sent. 1305 len. 35]: How much of wretchedness and starvation has been suffered in our own country within these few years , which , if our people had not been living abroad , might never have been felt !
Parsing [sent. 1306 len. 8]: Where are the elite of our aristocracy ?
Parsing [sent. 1307 len. 22]: Where are our country gentlemen who used to keep open house at their estates , disseminating their wealth and producing happiness ?
Parsing [sent. 1308 len. 39]: All driven abroad -- society disjointed -- no leader of fashion to set the example , by luxurious entertainments , of disseminating that wealth which ultimately finds its way into the greasy pocket of the labourer or mechanic .
Parsing [sent. 1309 len. 7]: Shops opened late and closed early .
Parsing [sent. 1310 len. 12]: Gin palaces , like hell , ever open to a customer .
Parsing [sent. 1311 len. 15]: The pulse of London hardly beats -- it is perceptible , but no more .
Parsing [sent. 1312 len. 13]: Nothing is active but the press , and the pressure from without .
Parsing [sent. 1313 len. 28]: But who would remain ten days in London in the month of November , when he can go away , without he had serious thoughts of suicide ?
Parsing [sent. 1314 len. 28]: Candles at high noon , yellow fogs , and torches in mid-day , do not suit me , so I 'm off again to a purer atmosphere .
Parsing [sent. 1315 len. 4]: CHAPTER TWENTY TWO .
Parsing [sent. 1316 len. 5]: Spa , June 30 .
Parsing [sent. 1317 len. 34]: Yesterday I fell in with two old friends , who , from a mere `` truant disposition , '' joined perhaps with a little good will towards me , came over to Spa .
Parsing [sent. 1318 len. 22]: As soon as their arrival had been announced , I went to them , and at their request joined their dinner .
Parsing [sent. 1319 len. 34]: After our first greetings , B -- , who not only appears , but really is , a man of fashion , in the best sense of the term , wanted his snuff-box .
Parsing [sent. 1320 len. 24]: It was in his bed-room , and his bed-room was locked by the servant , who had taken the key and gone out .
Parsing [sent. 1321 len. 20]: The consequence was , that B -- had to wait some time , and until the man came back .
Parsing [sent. 1322 len. 87]: I have always had a great aversion to a valet when constantly moving about on the Continent , as a single man ; and , although I do not now , as I used to do when a midshipman , brush my own clothes and black my own shoes , yet I like independence , in every thing , and infinitely prefer doing anything myself , to being waited upon ; for , generally speaking , it is the master who waits and not the man .
Parsing [sent. 1323 len. 30]: `` I wonder you bother yourself with such a travelling appendage , B -- , '' observed I , giving him a pinch of snuff to quiet his impatience .
Parsing [sent. 1324 len. 10]: `` I have never lately travelled with one . ''
Parsing [sent. 1325 len. 15]: `` My dear fellow -- the comfort of it -- you have no idea .
Parsing [sent. 1326 len. 11]: It would be impossible to get on without one . ''
Parsing [sent. 1327 len. 13]: `` Quite impossible , '' observed W -- , my other acquaintance .
Parsing [sent. 1328 len. 22]: `` I have been brought up in a school in which the word impossible has been erased from the language . ''
Parsing [sent. 1329 len. 9]: `` Well , but the comfort of it .
Parsing [sent. 1330 len. 21]: When you arrive , dirty and dusty , your portmanteau opened , all your articles of dress laid out . ''
Parsing [sent. 1331 len. 32]: `` I can do all that myself sooner than he can ; and , as I must wait till it be done , I may as well do it myself . ''
Parsing [sent. 1332 len. 29]: `` Yes , so you may , but then the security ; every thing locked up , which , in a strange hotel , is so necessary . ''
Parsing [sent. 1333 len. 18]: I lock my own room , and know where to find the key when I come in .
Parsing [sent. 1334 len. 17]: `` Very likely ; but still it is impossible to travel comfortably without a valet . ''
Parsing [sent. 1335 len. 9]: `` Quite impossible , '' rejoined W -- .
Parsing [sent. 1336 len. 15]: `` Be it so , '' replied I ; `` we differ in opinion .
Parsing [sent. 1337 len. 28]: All I can say is , that necessary as a valet is when stationary , he is a nuisance when you travel _ en garcon _ . ''
Parsing [sent. 1338 len. 41]: The conversation dropped , and we sat down to dinner ; the time passed away , as it always does , when old friends , who respect and like each other , meet , after an absence of some months .
Parsing [sent. 1339 len. 21]: After dinner we smoked cigars ; and , as the evening advanced , there were none left on the table .
Parsing [sent. 1340 len. 42]: B -- rang the bell for his servant to procure others ; the servant had gone out and was no where to be found , and for _ security _ had locked the bed-room door and taken the key with him .
Parsing [sent. 1341 len. 12]: So we drank our claret , and waited for his return .
Parsing [sent. 1342 len. 12]: `` Thinks I to myself '' -- but I said nothing .
Parsing [sent. 1343 len. 22]: At last , we waited till past twelve o'clock ; but the gentleman 's gentleman was no where to be found .
Parsing [sent. 1344 len. 17]: B -- was angry with the man , W -- had thrown himself on the sofa .
Parsing [sent. 1345 len. 38]: He wished to go to bed after a long day 's travel ; but his key was also , for security , in the valet 's pocket , who had been searched for every where without success .
Parsing [sent. 1346 len. 34]: B -- begged me not to remain out of politeness ; but I did remain not out of politeness , but of '' _ malice _ , '' as the French term it .
Parsing [sent. 1347 len. 23]: `` I had too much pleasure in their company to think of leaving them ; '' and we continued to sip brandy-and-water .
Parsing [sent. 1348 len. 28]: At last , three o'clock came , B -- was out of all patience , W -- snoring on the sofa , and I , quite delighted .
Parsing [sent. 1349 len. 16]: The sun should have poured his beams upon us before I would have gone away .
Parsing [sent. 1350 len. 17]: The bell was rung , but in vain , for the waiters would wait no longer .
Parsing [sent. 1351 len. 27]: It was proposed to send for a menuisier to pick the lock ; but how was one to be found at three o'clock in the morning ?
Parsing [sent. 1352 len. 17]: At last the valet , drunk and reeling in his morning jacket , entered the room .
Parsing [sent. 1353 len. 7]: `` The keys the keys ! ''
Parsing [sent. 1354 len. 6]: demanded B -- in wrath .
Parsing [sent. 1355 len. 5]: `` The key ! ''
Parsing [sent. 1356 len. 9]: roared W -- , who had woke up .
Parsing [sent. 1357 len. 19]: `` I have them , '' replied the valet , with a most knowing leer , facetiously smiling .
Parsing [sent. 1358 len. 13]: `` I have them -- all safe -- all right , gentlemen .
Parsing [sent. 1359 len. 26]: Here they are , '' continued the man , pulling them out , and presenting them as if he had done a very clever thing .
Parsing [sent. 1360 len. 9]: `` Here they are , you see . ''
Parsing [sent. 1361 len. 19]: The man was too tipsy to be expostulated with , and the gentlemen took their keys in silence .
Parsing [sent. 1362 len. 19]: `` And now , '' said I , `` gentlemen , I wish you a very good night .
Parsing [sent. 1363 len. 23]: You have fully established the extreme _ comfort _ of a travelling valet , and the impossibility of doing without one . ''
Parsing [sent. 1364 len. 43]: It was a glorious victory , although to get _ out _ of the house I had to open a window and leap from it , and to get _ into _ my own house at that hour was even more difficult .
Parsing [sent. 1365 len. 4]: CHAPTER TWENTY THREE .
Parsing [sent. 1366 len. 10]: I have been reading Jesse 's `` Gleanings . ''
Parsing [sent. 1367 len. 5]: Is he quite correct ?
Parsing [sent. 1368 len. 5]: I have my doubts .
Parsing [sent. 1369 len. 18]: In one point I certainly do not agree with him , in his favourite opinion of cats .
Parsing [sent. 1370 len. 55]: I do , however , know an instance of misplaced affection in a cat , which , although it does not add to the moral character of the race , is extremely curious for more reasons than one , and as it happened in my own family , I can vouch for its authenticity .
Parsing [sent. 1371 len. 19]: A little black spaniel had five puppies , which were considered too many for her to bring up .
Parsing [sent. 1372 len. 49]: As , however , the breed was much in request , her mistress was unwilling that any of them should be destroyed , and she asked the cook whether she thought it would be possible to bring a portion of them up by hand before the kitchen fire .
Parsing [sent. 1373 len. 28]: In reply , the cook observed that the cat had that day kittened , and that , perhaps , the puppies might be substituted for her progeny .
Parsing [sent. 1374 len. 17]: The experiment was made , two of the kittens were removed , and two puppies substituted .
Parsing [sent. 1375 len. 29]: The cat made no objections , took to them kindly , and gradually all the kittens were taken away , and the cat nursed the two puppies only .
Parsing [sent. 1376 len. 69]: Now , the first curious fact was , that the two puppies nursed by the cat were , in a fortnight , as active , forward , and playful , as kittens would have been : they had the use of their legs , barked , and gambolled about ; while the other three , nursed by the mother , were whining and rolling about like fat slugs .
Parsing [sent. 1377 len. 35]: The cat gave them her tail to play with , and they were always in motion ; they very soon ate meat , and long before the others they were fit to be removed .
Parsing [sent. 1378 len. 11]: This was done , and the cat became very inconsolable .
Parsing [sent. 1379 len. 28]: She prowled about the house , and on the second day of tribulation fell in with the little spaniel , who was nursing the other three puppies .
Parsing [sent. 1380 len. 5]: `` O ho ! ''
Parsing [sent. 1381 len. 19]: says Puss , putting up her back , `` it is you who have stolen my children . ''
Parsing [sent. 1382 len. 22]: `` No , '' replied the Spaniel , with a snarl , `` they are my own flesh and blood . ''
Parsing [sent. 1383 len. 30]: `` That wo n't do , '' said the cat , `` I 'll take my oath before any justice of peace that you have my two puppies . ''
Parsing [sent. 1384 len. 45]: Thereupon issue was joined , that is to say , there was a desperate combat , which ended in the defeat of the spaniel , and the cat walking proudly off with one of the puppies , which she took to her own bed .
Parsing [sent. 1385 len. 20]: Having deposited this one , she returned , fought again , gained another victory , and redeemed another puppy .
Parsing [sent. 1386 len. 22]: Now it is very singular that she should have only taken two , the exact number she had been deprived of .
Parsing [sent. 1387 len. 16]: Does this not prove to a certain extent the power of calculating numbers in animals ?
Parsing [sent. 1388 len. 39]: and does not the precocity of the two puppies brought up by the cat , infer there is some grounds for the supposition that with the milk is imbued much of the nature and disposition of the mother ?
Parsing [sent. 1389 len. 39]: A few experiments made on these points would be interesting , and we should have a new science , that of _ lacteology _ , to add to craniology , in our nurture and rearing of the species .
Parsing [sent. 1390 len. 11]: This reminds me of a singular fact , little known .
Parsing [sent. 1391 len. 36]: The Burmahs , who are disciples of Gaudma , equally with the inhabitants of Pegu and Syriam , whose country they have conquered , worship the White Elephant , who is considered as a god .
Parsing [sent. 1392 len. 17]: There have been but three white elephants since the foundation of the Burmah dynasty by Alompraa .
Parsing [sent. 1393 len. 26]: The first one is dead , and I have one of his teeth carved with figures , which was consecrated to the great Dagon Pagoda .
Parsing [sent. 1394 len. 36]: The second now _ reigns _ -- he is attended by hundreds , wears a howdah , or cloth , studded with precious stones ; which is said to be worth a million of money .
Parsing [sent. 1395 len. 17]: He also wears his bangles or armlets on each leg , and fares sumptuously every day .
Parsing [sent. 1396 len. 22]: White elephants are very scarce ; the colour is occasioned by a disease in the animal , a species of leprosy .
Parsing [sent. 1397 len. 31]: Any elephant hunter in these countries , who is fortunate enough to capture a white elephant , is immediately created a noble , and advanced to high honour and wealth .
Parsing [sent. 1398 len. 38]: The third white elephant , of which I am about to speak particularly , and who may be considered as the heir apparent , was taken a few months previous to our declaring war against the Burmahs .
Parsing [sent. 1399 len. 18]: He was very young ; his mother had been killed , and he yet required partial nourishment .
Parsing [sent. 1400 len. 59]: He was brought to Rangoon , established in one of the best houses in the place , and an edict was sent forth from the capital , ordering that twenty-four of the most healthy young married women should be dedicated to his wants , and if they fell off in powers of nourishment , be replaced by others .
Parsing [sent. 1401 len. 16]: This was considered an honour -- for were they not nursing a _ God _ ?
Parsing [sent. 1402 len. 59]: Major Canning , the political agent , who went to see this curious spectacle , described it to me as follows : `` The animal was not above three feet and a few inches high , its colour was a dirty grey , rather than white ; it was very healthy , playful , and in good spirits .
Parsing [sent. 1403 len. 41]: When I went into the room , which was very spacious , and built of teak-wood , the twenty-four nurses were sitting or lying on mats about the room , some playing at draughts and other games , others working .
Parsing [sent. 1404 len. 23]: The elephant walking about , looking at them , and what they were doing , as if he understood all about it .
Parsing [sent. 1405 len. 35]: After a short time , the little deity felt hungry , and , with his trunk he pushed some of the women , but to annoy him they would not yield to his solicitations .
Parsing [sent. 1406 len. 36]: When he became angry , and was too rough for them , they submitted , and he put his trunk round their waists in the most affectionate manner , while he was supplying himself . ''
Parsing [sent. 1407 len. 36]: I did not see the animal myself , as immediately that they heard of our arrival at the mouth of the river , they despatched him under a strong guard to a place of security .
Parsing [sent. 1408 len. 23]: But I should like to ascertain hereafter , whether his nurture made him a more reasonable being than are elephants in general .
Parsing [sent. 1409 len. 11]: How one 's thoughts fly away over time and space !
Parsing [sent. 1410 len. 21]: What a rush of incidents crowd into my memory , merely from having mentioned this circumstance of the white elephant .
Parsing [sent. 1411 len. 43]: I did once intend to have written a narrative of what passed during our sojourn in that country , for I saw more of the inhabitants than most people ; but others have forestalled me , and it is now too late .
Parsing [sent. 1412 len. 31]: Nevertheless , it will perhaps amuse the reader , if , without entering into the military details , I mention a few of the operations and scenes which then occurred .
Parsing [sent. 1413 len. 16]: It shall be so then , and we will discourse a little about the Burmahs .
Parsing [sent. 1414 len. 16]: An Armenian merchant who resided there told me a story one day which was curious .
Parsing [sent. 1415 len. 22]: The King of Pegu was possessed of the most splendid ruby in the world , both as to size and colour .
Parsing [sent. 1416 len. 13]: This was well known ; it was the boast of the nation .
Parsing [sent. 1417 len. 44]: When the Burmahs subdued the kingdom of Pegu , the old king with all his family were taken prisoners , vast treasure was also captured , but the great ruby was not to be found , notwithstanding the torture and beheading of thousands .
Parsing [sent. 1418 len. 37]: With the usual barbarity of these countries , the old king , a miserable paralytic little man , was stripped naked and confined in an iron cage , which I saw when I was at Rangoon .
Parsing [sent. 1419 len. 26]: In this confinement he lived for ten or twelve years , every festival day being brought out and exposed to the derision of the populace .
Parsing [sent. 1420 len. 22]: At last he died , and his body was thrown out to be devoured by the dogs and birds of prey .
Parsing [sent. 1421 len. 58]: One of the soldiers who assisted to drag the body out of the cage , turned it over with his foot , and perceived that his right hand grasped a hump of _ damma _ , -LRB- a sort of pitch , -RRB- which curiosity induced the Burmah to force out with the point of his spear .
Parsing [sent. 1422 len. 49]: This had been observed before , but the Burmahs , who are very superstitions and carry about them all sorts of charms , imagined it to be a charm for his paralysis or palsy with which he was afflicted , and therefore had allowed him to retain it .
Parsing [sent. 1423 len. 67]: But when the Burmah took it up , the weight of it convinced him that it was not all damma : he examined it , and found that it was the great ruby of the Pegu kingdom which had been lost , and which the old man had for so many years , in a state of nudity and incarceration , held in his left hand .
Parsing [sent. 1424 len. 75]: I asked one of the Burmah chiefs whether this ruby now in the possession of the King of Ava was so fine as represented : his answer was in truly Eastern hyperbole -- `` Dip it in the Irrawaddy , '' said he , -LRB- that is , an enormous river seven hundred miles long and in many parts several miles broad , -RRB- `` and the whole water will turn to blood . ''
Parsing [sent. 1425 len. 36]: I have said that the Burmahs are very superstitious : they have a great variety of charms which they wear about their persons , but there is one custom of theirs which is very singular .
Parsing [sent. 1426 len. 37]: They polish rubies ; that is , without cutting them in _ facettes _ , but merely the stone , whatever its primitive shape , is rubbed down on every side until it is perfectly smooth .
Parsing [sent. 1427 len. 35]: They then make an incision in the flesh , generally the arm or leg , put in the ruby and allow the skin to heal over it , so that the stone remains there .
Parsing [sent. 1428 len. 66]: Soldiers and sailors in search of plunder will find out any thing , and this practice of the Burmahs was soon discovered ; and after the assault and carrying of a stockade , you would see the men passing their hands over the bodies , and immediately they felt a rising in the limb , out with their knives and cut in for the rubies .
Parsing [sent. 1429 len. 23]: Indeed , the plunder was more considerable than might be imagined , for every Burmah carried all his wealth about his person .
Parsing [sent. 1430 len. 12]: Another singular custom arising from their superstition prevails among this people .
Parsing [sent. 1431 len. 46]: The king has a corps denominated _ Invulnerables _ , whose ranks are filled up in this manner : -- when a criminal is condemned to death for certain offences , such as robbery , he is permitted to challenge as an _ invulnerable _ .
Parsing [sent. 1432 len. 20]: This is proved by his standing at a certain distance from several men who fire at him with ball .
Parsing [sent. 1433 len. 19]: Should he not be wounded or killed , he is pronounced an invulnerable and enrolled in the corps .
Parsing [sent. 1434 len. 27]: In every stockade we attacked , there were always one or two of these men , and they really appeared to believe in their own powers .
Parsing [sent. 1435 len. 37]: They generally stood above the timbers of the stockade , dancing and capering as the boats advanced , and continued their extravagance amidst a shower of bullets , exposing their persons in a most undaunted manner .
Parsing [sent. 1436 len. 113]: There was one fellow who , dressed in a short red jacket , and nothing else except the cloth round his loins , who was well known to our men ; they called him _ Happy Jack _ , from the capers which he used to cut , and somehow or another it was his good fortune never to be hit , at least , not that we know of , for taking stockade after stockade , at every fresh attack there was Happy Jack to be seen capering and shouting as usual , and never ceasing to expose himself until the troops had landed and were about to scale the fortress .
Parsing [sent. 1437 len. 24]: It was quite amusing to hear the men shout out with laughter , `` By heavens , there 's Happy Jack again . ''
Parsing [sent. 1438 len. 18]: I hope he is alive at this moment ; at all events , he deserves to be .
Parsing [sent. 1439 len. 4]: CHAPTER TWENTY FOUR .
Parsing [sent. 1440 len. 2]: Spa .
Parsing [sent. 1441 len. 88]: Yes , now Spa is agreeable : we have no _ redoubte _ open with fools losing their money , no English _ passants _ looking after amusement , no valetudinarians drinking the _ poupon _ , no Spa boxes crowding every window : we are now as a Spa should be , a _ coterie _ of houses in a ravine , surrounded by the mountains of the Ardennes , crowding and shoving up together in mutual protection against the deep snow and the forest wolves .
Parsing [sent. 1442 len. 53]: There is something new in this : most of the houses are shut up ; the shop-windows are all bare ; the snow is two feet deep in the streets ; the mountains on every side are white ; the icicles hang upon the leafless boughs , and the rivulets are enchained .
Parsing [sent. 1443 len. 132]: All is one drear blank ; and except the two-horse diligence which heaves slowly in sight three or four hours past its time , and the post , -LRB- which is now delivered at nine o'clock instead of noon -RRB- ; there is no such thing as an arrival : the boys slide upon their little sledges down the hills ; the cattle are driven home ; the church clock strikes ; and unless we are enlivened by the crowd assembled round the countryman , who appears with the carcass of a wolf which he has been fortunate enough to kill , we are all quiet , monotony and peace : in fact , Spa , now that it is a desert , has become to me , at least agreeable .
Parsing [sent. 1444 len. 25]: They say , this hard winter promises plenty of wolves ; if so , I recommend those who are fond of excitement come here .
Parsing [sent. 1445 len. 20]: Indeed , it will be profitable , for if they are active huntsmen , they can pay their expenses .
Parsing [sent. 1446 len. 35]: A dead horse costs little , and in Spa , as they give very little to the horses to eat in summer , and nothing at all in the winter , they die fast .
Parsing [sent. 1447 len. 27]: You have only to drag the carcass to an outhouse at a little distance from the town , and with your rifle watch during the night .
Parsing [sent. 1448 len. 35]: The wolves will come down to prey upon the carrion , and it is hard if you do not kill your couple during the night , and then you are rewarded by the commune .
Parsing [sent. 1449 len. 39]: I do not know what the price is now , but when the King of Holland was in possession of Belgium it was one hundred francs for a male , and three hundred francs for a female wolf .
Parsing [sent. 1450 len. 34]: Now a brace a night , four hundred francs , or sixteen pounds , is not a bad night 's earning : in Spa it would keep a half-pay officer for three months .
Parsing [sent. 1451 len. 38]: There is a curious story here , proving the sagacity of a wolf which came down an hour before dusk into the town , and made off with a child of two years old in her mouth .
Parsing [sent. 1452 len. 10]: The cry was raised , and the pursuit immediate .
Parsing [sent. 1453 len. 33]: After following her track for many miles , she gained upon them , it became quite dark , and the people returned homewards , melancholy at the fate of the poor child .
Parsing [sent. 1454 len. 38]: When they were about half way back , they heard the wail of an infant , and , guided by it , they arrived at a thick bush , where they found the child alive and unhurt .
Parsing [sent. 1455 len. 32]: The wolf , finding that her pursuers gained upon her , had deposited the child there , intending to return and make a meal of it upon a more favourable opportunity .
Parsing [sent. 1456 len. 22]: We have had nothing to excite us within these last few days but the death and burial of an old curate .
Parsing [sent. 1457 len. 17]: He died in all the odour of sanctity three days ago , and was buried yesterday .
Parsing [sent. 1458 len. 19]: He was not loved or even liked , for he wanted that greatest of all gifts -- charity .
Parsing [sent. 1459 len. 61]: His situation was worth , with offerings , six thousand francs a year , -- a large sum in this country : but he did not give to the poor ; he exacted from them , and they religiously obeyed him , no one killing a pig or anything else without a present of part of it to the curate .
Parsing [sent. 1460 len. 19]: When the old man was told that he could not live , the ruling passion still governed him .
Parsing [sent. 1461 len. 31]: He sent for a person to dispose of for him the sundry pieces of pork which he had gathered as presents , then took the extreme unction , and died .
Parsing [sent. 1462 len. 45]: His will is not known , but he is supposed to be very rich , and whether he leaves his wealth to some nephews , or to support a hospital here which is at present without funds , is a question of some interest .
Parsing [sent. 1463 len. 15]: He was buried in great parade and procession , followed by hundreds holding candles .
Parsing [sent. 1464 len. 24]: He was dressed in his best , and every one said that he never looked so clean or so well in his life .
Parsing [sent. 1465 len. 36]: He was carried on an open _ brancard _ , with his canonical hat on his head , the snow fell fast and settled on his face and clothes , but he felt it not .
Parsing [sent. 1466 len. 19]: The funeral was as cold as his charity , the thermometer being exactly 130 below the freezing point .
Parsing [sent. 1467 len. 26]: Except the procession of the dead curate and of a dead wolf , we have had nothing to interest us for the last ten days .
Parsing [sent. 1468 len. 9]: But I promised to talk about the Burmahs .
Parsing [sent. 1469 len. 84]: There have been two or three accounts of the military movements , but there has been no inquiry or examination into the character of the people , which , in my opinion , is of more importance than is generally supposed ; for although the East India Company may imagine that they have done with the Burmahs , it is my conviction that the Burmahs have not done with them , and even I may live to witness the truth of my assertion .
Parsing [sent. 1470 len. 29]: It certainly is a point of some interest to ascertain from whence the Burmah nation originally came : that they are not aborigines , I think most certain .
Parsing [sent. 1471 len. 31]: They are surrounded by the Cochin Chinese , the Chinese , and the Hindoos , all races of inferior stature and effeminate in person , with little or no beard .
Parsing [sent. 1472 len. 36]: Now the Burmahs are a very powerful race , very muscular in their limbs , possessing great strength and energy : generally speaking , I should say , that they are rather taller than Europeans .
Parsing [sent. 1473 len. 38]: They have the high cheek bones of the Tatar , but not the small eyes ; they have strong hair and beards , and certainly would remind you of a cross between the Jew and the Tatar .
Parsing [sent. 1474 len. 62]: This is singular ; and it gave the idea to some of those who are fond of indulging in theory , that they might be the remnants of that portion of the Jews who , when permitted to leave Babylon , instead of going east with the others , bent their course to the westward and were never spoken of afterwards .
Parsing [sent. 1475 len. 43]: But the only props they had to this argument were the appearance of the people , the weight in silver being called the _ tekel _ or shekel , and the great pagoda having the name of the _ Dagon _ pagoda .
Parsing [sent. 1476 len. 31]: At least I heard of no more to support the argument but those three , which can hardly be sufficient , although the coincidence of the two words is singular .
Parsing [sent. 1477 len. 49]: The Burmahs are semi-barbarous : but this term must be used in the most favourable light ; because , surrounded on every side by people who are wedded to their own customs , the Burmahs have a liberality and a desire to improve , which is very remarkable .
Parsing [sent. 1478 len. 73]: I never met with any Burmah , not even a lad , who could not read and write ; they allow any form of religion to be made use of , and churches of any description to be built by foreigners , but they do not like missionaries making converts of their own people ; for as the king is the head of the religion , conversion is a breach of allegiance .
Parsing [sent. 1479 len. 18]: One of the missionaries had an audience with the king , and demanded permission to make proselytes .
Parsing [sent. 1480 len. 25]: The king replied that the missionary might convert as many as he pleased , but that he would cut all their heads off afterwards .
Parsing [sent. 1481 len. 22]: The missionary had not much trouble , when this answer was made known , in counting the heads of his proselytes .
Parsing [sent. 1482 len. 28]: In their own religion , which is Budhism , the Burmahs appear to be very relax ; it is too absurd for the energy of their minds .
Parsing [sent. 1483 len. 32]: Those who enter the priesthood wear a yellow dress ; but if a priest at any time feels disposed to quit his profession , he is at liberty so to do .
Parsing [sent. 1484 len. 24]: All he has to do is to throw off his yellow garment ; but at the same time he can never resume it .
Parsing [sent. 1485 len. 15]: The Burmahs are superstitious about charms , but are not superstitious on religious points .
Parsing [sent. 1486 len. 55]: In fact , there is very little religion among them , and had we , at the close of the war , instead of demanding a crore of rupees , insisted that they should embrace Christianity , the king would have given the order , and the whole nation would have nominally been Christians .
Parsing [sent. 1487 len. 15]: I once asked a Burmah soldier what was his idea of a future state .
Parsing [sent. 1488 len. 49]: His idea of bliss was singular -- `` I shall be turned into a buffalo , and shall lie down in a meadow of grass higher than my head , and eat all day long , and there wo n't be a single mosquito to annoy me . ''
Parsing [sent. 1489 len. 55]: While on the subject of religion , I may here observe , that at the capture of Rangoon I entered a Chinese temple , the altar-piece , if I may use the term , was the Ganesa of the Hindoos , but not seated on the lotus leaf , but on the Chinese rat .
Parsing [sent. 1490 len. 24]: On each side of this were two little candelabras , formed of the Egyptian ibis , holding the oil cups in its beak .
Parsing [sent. 1491 len. 17]: I also found the Hounyman , or monkey god of the Hindoos , and Budhist figures .
Parsing [sent. 1492 len. 63]: I once observed some sepoys playing and laughing at a bronze image they had picked up at the pagoda of Syriam , and on examining it , I was surprised to find that it was a figure of the Egyptian Isis , with her hand raised , and her person in the position described as the correct one when blessing the world .
Parsing [sent. 1493 len. 20]: The art of embalming appears to be known to the Burmahs , and is occasionally practised by the priests .
Parsing [sent. 1494 len. 45]: At the capture of the old Portuguese fort at Syriam , I found , not far from it , a sort of canopied shed , decorated with carving , cut paper , and tinsel , and supported by four pillars , like a bedstead .
Parsing [sent. 1495 len. 12]: Below lay the body of a priest , embalmed and gilt .
Parsing [sent. 1496 len. 47]: I intended to have brought this home , but before I arrived there , I found one of my marines , a graceless dog without religion or any other good quality , very busy hammering the mummy to pieces with the butt end of his musket .
Parsing [sent. 1497 len. 11]: I was very angry , and ordered him to desist .
Parsing [sent. 1498 len. 43]: In excuse , he replied that it was an abominable molten image , and it was his duty , as a _ good Christian _ , to destroy it -- the only evidence of Christianity ever witnessed on that fellow 's part .
Parsing [sent. 1499 len. 83]: On examination , I found that the body had been wrapped in sundry clothes , and , like the ark of Noah , pitched within and without : over the clothes was a coat of damma , then of chunam , and lastly it was gilt ; the head of the mummy was fictitious , and formed of a cocoa-nut , the real skull being where , in the mummy , would have appeared to have been the breast of the body .
Parsing [sent. 1500 len. 28]: It did not smell much , but there were a great many small scarabei inside , and it was so mutilated that I did not remove it .
Parsing [sent. 1501 len. 38]: The Burmahs are cleanly in their houses , which generally are raised from the ground a few feet , so as to allow the pigs ; which are the scavengers of the town , to walk under .
Parsing [sent. 1502 len. 37]: They have houses of brick , or stone and mortar , such as the custom-house at Rangoon , and one or two others ; but the most substantial houses are usually built of thick teak plank .
Parsing [sent. 1503 len. 48]: The smaller houses and cottages are built of bamboo , the floors and walls being woven like wicker-work : the cleanliness and the beauty of these houses when new are very remarkable , and what is still more so , the rapidity with which they are built .
Parsing [sent. 1504 len. 47]: I have known an officer order a house to be built of three rooms , with doors and windows to each , and of a comfortable size , and three or four Burmahs will complete this house in a day , and thatch the roof over .
Parsing [sent. 1505 len. 34]: In another point , the Burmahs show a degree of civilisation , which might be an example to the northern Athens -- to every house there is a very neat and clean cloaca .
Parsing [sent. 1506 len. 37]: The government , like all in Asia , is most despotic ; and the people have the faults which are certain to be generated by despotism -- but not to that degree which might be expected .
Parsing [sent. 1507 len. 16]: They have their hereditary nobility , and the orders of it are very clearly defined .
Parsing [sent. 1508 len. 60]: They consist of gold chains , worn round the neck , with four plates or chased bosses dividing them ; the lowest order wears the bosses linked together by three chains , the next highest in degree with six , the next nine , and the last and highest order has twelve ; the king only wears twenty-four chains .
Parsing [sent. 1509 len. 20]: The use of gold and silver , as drinking cups , etcetera , is only permitted to the nobility .
Parsing [sent. 1510 len. 44]: They are very clever in chasing of metals , and they have a description of work in glass and enamel , quite their own , with which they decorate the temples , houses of the priests , and coffers containing the sacred volumes .
Parsing [sent. 1511 len. 33]: Their ornamental writings in the Pali language , a variety of the Sanscrit , known only to the priests , are also very beautiful -- especially that upon long leaves of ivory .
Parsing [sent. 1512 len. 18]: Upon the whole , their manufactures are superior to all around them , except perhaps the Chinese .
Parsing [sent. 1513 len. 49]: The women are small , and delicately formed , in proportion to the men ; they are not shut up , but go where they please ; their dress is becoming ; they braid the hair with flowers , and they are much fairer than would be supposed .
Parsing [sent. 1514 len. 13]: Those who keep much within doors are nearly as white as Europeans .
Parsing [sent. 1515 len. 47]: They have a singular custom of putting a patch of white chunam on the cheek bone , something in opposition to the black patches which used formerly to be worn by our belles ; and it is intended to show how near they approach to white .
Parsing [sent. 1516 len. 45]: Indeed , when the men of the lower class , who are exposed all day to the sun , remove their garments , it is singular to witness how many shades lighter they are in that part of their bodies which is covered up .
Parsing [sent. 1517 len. 15]: Usually , the men have but one wife , but occasionally there are supernumeraries .
Parsing [sent. 1518 len. 30]: The laws of the Burmahs appear to be good , but , as in all despotic countries , they are not acted upon , unless it please the ruler .
Parsing [sent. 1519 len. 8]: Slavery of a certain species is allowed .
Parsing [sent. 1520 len. 64]: Should one man be in debt to another , and is summoned before the chief ; if he states his inability to pay , he is asked how many children he has , and according to the debt , so are his children given in bond slavery to his debtor , who writes off a certain sum every year until they are free .
Parsing [sent. 1521 len. 21]: If he has no children , his wife , or himself perhaps , will be bonded in the same manner .
Parsing [sent. 1522 len. 69]: But in this case , where ill-treatment can be proved , the bondage will be removed ; and further , any person so bonded , may at his or her wish remove to the service of another master , provided they can find one who will pay to the debtor the amount still due , and thus finish the time of servitude under one whom they like better .
Parsing [sent. 1523 len. 12]: These bonds are all in writing , and must be produced .
Parsing [sent. 1524 len. 15]: Some of our military officers released several of the young women from their slavery .
Parsing [sent. 1525 len. 19]: _ Sitting down _ in your presence , is , among the Burmese , a mark of respect .
Parsing [sent. 1526 len. 26]: Every poor man who is sent for , immediately drops down on his hams in the corner of the room , or at the portal .
Parsing [sent. 1527 len. 28]: The use of the cocoa , or betel nut , is universal among the men , but not so common with the women until they grow old .
Parsing [sent. 1528 len. 26]: The consequence is , that the teeth of the men are quite black and decayed , while those of the young women are very good .
Parsing [sent. 1529 len. 30]: The most remarkable feature in the character of the Burmahs is their _ good temper _ ; I think they are the most even-tempered race , ever met with .
Parsing [sent. 1530 len. 11]: They are always gay , always content under any privation .
Parsing [sent. 1531 len. 34]: I had , as will be seen hereafter , more opportunities of seeing into the character of this people than others had , for we mixed with them in amity for some weeks .
Parsing [sent. 1532 len. 17]: They are very fond of marionettes , and puppet playing , and are very amusing mimics .
Parsing [sent. 1533 len. 11]: They work very hard , and with the greatest cheerfulness .
Parsing [sent. 1534 len. 51]: They have a high respect for the English , or the white faces , as they call us ; and the superiority of our warlike instruments , and our ships , _ was _ a subject of wonder , and , at the same time , of most careful examination .
Parsing [sent. 1535 len. 16]: They perceive how far they are behind us , and are most anxious to improve .
Parsing [sent. 1536 len. 69]: From this reason , joined to others , it was a pity that we ever made war with the Burmahs ; they had made an easy conquest of those around them , and were satisfied with their supposed superiority , but now they are not , for they are active and enterprising , fond of war , and will not be content until they have improved their system .
Parsing [sent. 1537 len. 76]: Twenty years hence we shall find the Burmahs a much more formidable nation than they are at present , for they have every quality necessary to become the first nation in the East : indeed , when we consider with what weapons they defended themselves , and the nature of the warfare , it is not a little to their credit that they held out for nearly three years against the power of Great Britain .
Parsing [sent. 1538 len. 4]: CHAPTER TWENTY FIVE .
Parsing [sent. 1539 len. 4]: February , 1836 .
Parsing [sent. 1540 len. 24]: The Burmahs are decidedly a brave nation : the government being despotic , their rulers are cruel , but the people are not .
Parsing [sent. 1541 len. 14]: I state this , as cowardice and cruelty usually go hand in hand .
Parsing [sent. 1542 len. 21]: Good temper and generosity are the prominent features in their character -- excellent materials to work upon in judicious hands .
Parsing [sent. 1543 len. 40]: I witnessed acts of courage at the early part of the war , before the Burmahs found out how impossible it was to cope with our superior arms , which were most surprising , and which excited our admiration .
Parsing [sent. 1544 len. 15]: They are peculiarly a warlike nation ; indeed , they are fond of war .
Parsing [sent. 1545 len. 26]: Every man is a soldier , and when ordered out to join the ranks , obeys without receiving any pay , providing his own arms .
Parsing [sent. 1546 len. 14]: This fact , at once , establishes that they are inclined to war .
Parsing [sent. 1547 len. 47]: Their aims generally consist of a double-handed sword , a weapon of great force , and very large spears ; but every one will possess a musket if he can , and if it has not a lock , he will fire it with a match .
Parsing [sent. 1548 len. 54]: It is in this point that the Burmahs are so deficient in aims : we used to consider it a very courageous act to venture to fire off a Burmese musket , they were in such a wretched condition : and to crown all , every man _ makes his own gunpowder _ .
Parsing [sent. 1549 len. 37]: Now it may be easily imagined what stuff this must be ; as , previous to an expected combat , each Burmah sits down and composes the article to the best of his knowledge and belief .
Parsing [sent. 1550 len. 42]: The consequences are , that when these muskets do go off -LRB- and it is ten to one they do not -RRB- , it is again ten to one that the bullet falls short , from the inefficacy of the powder .
Parsing [sent. 1551 len. 34]: There is another singular fact , and one which proves that they have been used to muskets but a short time : it is , that they have no bullet-moulds or leaden bullets .
Parsing [sent. 1552 len. 39]: All their bullets are of iron , hammered as round as they can hammer them at the forge ; of course the windage produced by this imperfect shape , occasions it to deviate much from its intended direction .
Parsing [sent. 1553 len. 20]: The guns on their stockades and war-boats are equally defective from bad powder , and the hammered iron bullets .
Parsing [sent. 1554 len. 15]: It is difficult to know where they could have collected such a curious assemblage .
Parsing [sent. 1555 len. 30]: Sometimes you will fall in with a small brass piece of exquisite Spanish manufacture , at others you will find them of the strangest forms that can be conceived .
Parsing [sent. 1556 len. 21]: I rather think they were purchased , or taken as a part of the duties on vessels trading to Rangoon .
Parsing [sent. 1557 len. 29]: I recollect once at the first taking of a stockade , we knocked off the trunnions of an old iron gun , and left it there as useless .
Parsing [sent. 1558 len. 46]: The Burmahs reoccupied the stockade , and we had to take it a second time , when we found that they had most ingeniously supplied the want of trunnions with iron hoops and rivets , and the gun was fired at us before we entered .
Parsing [sent. 1559 len. 43]: At another time , we entered a stockade which had kept up a brisk fire for a few minutes , and to our surprise found that they had made _ wooden _ guns , very well bound and braced with iron hoops .
Parsing [sent. 1560 len. 57]: Of course these guns would not fire more than two or three shots each , as the touch-holes became inflamed , and were soon so large as to render the guns unserviceable ; but I mention these points , to prove the perseverance of these people , and the efforts they made in their own defence .
Parsing [sent. 1561 len. 70]: After the first campaign it is true that they deserted , and the levies were made by force ; but the reason of this , for I inquired into it , was not that they had any objection to fight , but that , fighting without pay , they wanted to go home and put the seed into the ground , as otherwise their wives and families would starve .
Parsing [sent. 1562 len. 35]: The Burmah war-boats are very splendid craft , pulling from eighty to one hundred oars ; the Burmahs manage them very dexterously , and will pull them from seven to eight miles an hour .
Parsing [sent. 1563 len. 42]: They have a war-boat dedicated to the Deity , which brought intelligence that saved the nation at the time of the war with the empire of Pegu , in a space of time so short , as almost to appear incredible .
Parsing [sent. 1564 len. 25]: As I before observed , the gun mounted on the boat 's bow is of little effect , but their spears are really formidable .
Parsing [sent. 1565 len. 33]: At a night attack upon some of our vessels , anchored off a stockade which they wanted to regain , I had an evidence of the force with which they are thrown .
Parsing [sent. 1566 len. 40]: The sides of the vessels were covered with them , sticking out like porcupine 's quills , and they had entered the plank with such force , that it required a very strong arm to pull them out again .
Parsing [sent. 1567 len. 40]: We lost some men by them ; the effect of a hundred spears hurtling through the air at the same time was singularly appalling to our men , who were not accustomed the sound , especially during the night .
Parsing [sent. 1568 len. 35]: I heard several of the sailors observe afterwards that they `` did not like that at all , '' and I am sure they would have infinitely preferred to have been met with fire-arms .
Parsing [sent. 1569 len. 26]: Some of these spears were sixteen feet long , with an iron head , sharp at both sides , weighing from twelve to fourteen pounds .
Parsing [sent. 1570 len. 27]: I have seen bows and arrows in the possession of the Burmahs , but never have observed that they used them in their conflicts with us .
Parsing [sent. 1571 len. 6]: They appeared to despise them .
Parsing [sent. 1572 len. 21]: The system of warfare and defence pursued by these people , is undoubtedly excellent for the peculiarities of the country .
Parsing [sent. 1573 len. 42]: Their stockades are usually built of any thick teak timber , or rather squared trees , which are much too strong to be penetrated by any other than battering cannon , and , in consequence , were invariably carried by escalade .
Parsing [sent. 1574 len. 18]: Some of them are built of bamboos , running from a foot to two feet in diameter .
Parsing [sent. 1575 len. 28]: These are equally strong , with the peculiarity that if you fire cannon at them the bamboos yield , admit the shot , and then close again .
Parsing [sent. 1576 len. 51]: If these stockades are not close to the river side , they usually have a deep ditch round them , and are further protected by what was more serious to us than the escalading , which were abbatis of pointed bamboos , stuck in a slanting direction in the ground .
